[DOB-124] - Admission (Discharged) in NH PAV Periop Services (continued)
OP Notes (continued)
operative suite. After the satisfactory induction of general anesthesia,the
operative extremity was prepped and draped in a normal sterile manner.
Surgical time-out was then called to confirm that the patient had been given
appropriate preoperative antibiotics, that this was the correct patient, correct
procedure, and correct operative extremity.
A posterior portal was established in the glenohumeral joint was entered. An
anterior portal was established.
The underside of the rotator cuff is intact. The articular cartilage of the
glenohumeral joint was intact. As predicted on the MRI there was a discrete
anterior attachment of the labrum at the 9 o'clock position. The bicep tendon and
anchor were intact. An arthroscopic Freer was used to dissect the area of the
tear and then a rasp was used to abrade the anterior bony glenoid.
The labrum was then reapproximated using a single bioabsorbable suture
anchor.
An accessory superior lateral portal was established and scope was placed in the
subacromial space. A complete subacromial bursectomy was performed and
then the shaver was used to remove the underlying acromial spur. The top side
of the rotator cuff was intact
All fluid and soft tissue debris was drained from the joint. The portals were closed
with nylon, and covered with a dry sterile dressing.
The patient tolerated the procedure well and was returned to the recovery room
in satisfactory condition
8/10/2020 1:35 PM
Cyna Khalily, MD

Procedure: Interscalene Nerve Block
Reason for Block/Indications: at surgeon's request and post-op pain management
The procedure and alternatives were discussed as well as all clinically relevant risks and benefits. All questions were
answered. The patient (and/or proxy) agreed to proceed, informed consent obtained
Sedation: IV sedation, See MAR for details
(NH 113-149 sec) (AUD,NWC,NBH, 123-172 sec) (Pediatric 89-169 sec)Laterality: Left
Procedure timeout performed
Procedure site has been marked and confirmed by Anesthesia Provider
Patient position: Sitting
Prep: Chlorhexidine.
Procedure Technique: Ultrasound guided. Ultrasound used to visualize needle placement in proximity to nerve being
blocked.
Needle type: Stimuplex 10 G 20 cm
Start time: 8/10/2020 11:46 AM
End time: 8/10/2020 11:47 AM
Injection made incrementally with aspirations every 5 mL.
Additional Notes: Patient was identified, consent checked, and timeout performed. Patient was interviewed and risks
and benefits of anesthesia and peripheral nerve block were discussed prior to procedure, and patient was in
agreement. In addition to the description above, the procedure was performed as follows:
1) Under ultrasound guidance, a 20 gauge needle was inserted and placed in close proximity to the brachial plexus at
the interscalene level.
2) Ultrasound was also used to visualize the spread of anesthetic in close proximity to the nerve being blocked.
3) The nerve appeared anatomically normal.

Adm: 8/10/2020, D/C: 8/10/2020
[DOB-108] - Admission (Discharged) in NH PAV Periop Services (continued)
Anesthesia on 08/10/20 (continued)
Procedure Technique: Ultrasound guided. Ultrasound used to visualize needle placement in proximity to nerve being
blocked.
Needle type: Stimuplex 10 G 20 cm
Start time: 8/10/2020 11:46 AM
End time: 8/10/2020 11:47 AM
Injection made incrementally with aspirations every 5 mL.
Additional Notes: Patient was identified, consent checked, and timeout performed. Patient was interviewed and risks
and benefits of anesthesia and peripheral nerve block were discussed prior to procedure, and patient was in
agreement. In addition to the description above, the procedure was performed as follows:
1) Under ultrasound guidance, a 20 gauge needle was inserted and placed in close proximity to the brachial plexus at
the interscalene level.
2) Ultrasound was also used to visualize the spread of anesthetic in close proximity to the nerve being blocked.
3) The nerve appeared anatomically normal.
4) There were no apparent abnormal pathological findings.
5) A permanent ultrasound image was saved to the patient's record.
There were no apparent complications, and patient was conversant throughout procedure. Patient tolerated procedure
well. Please see MAR for drug dosages and times.

and peripheral nerve block were discussed prior to procedure, and patient

performed as follows:

close proximity to the brachial plexus at the interscalene level.
2) Ultrasound was also used to visualize the spread of anesthetic in close
proximity to the nerve being blocked.
3) The nerve appeared anatomically normal.
4) There were no apparent abnormal pathological findings.
5) A permanent ultrasound image was saved to the patient's record.
There were no apparent complications, and patient was conversant
throughout procedure. Patient tolerated procedure well. Please see MAR
for drug dosages and times.

Topic: Disease Management - PostOp General Surgery (Resolved)
Point: Special Care Needs Related to Specific Surgery (Specify in Comments or Add Teaching Point) (Resolved)
Point: Incision/Wound Care (Resolved)
Know how to care for your wound. Emphasize good hand hygiene before and after caring for the the wound.
Teach about signs and symptoms of infection and when to notify healthcare provider.
Teach to tell family and friends to never touch wound or bandage and to clean their hands before and after visiting.
Instruct to keep incision/wound as clean and dry as possible.
Caution against: scrubbing or rubbing the incision, removing the tape strips, using lotion or powder around the incision,
exposing the incision to sunlight, taking a bath unless the incision can be kept dry.
Point: Edema Management (Resolved)
Description:
Description:
Educate patient/family/caregiver on how to care for incision/wound to include: how to clean, when to clean and any special
instruction for cleaning.
Educate patient/family/caregiver that patient may get puffy and look swollen. Need to reposition frequently, elevate
extremities above heart level if possible, use ice packs as ordered, maintain fluid and diet control.
Description:
Educate patient/family/caregiver on the specific care needs, reason, how to perform and expected length of time needed
due to surgery.

Medication Information
Preparation for Your Discharge:
Your providers may have already given you your prescription for pain medication prior to your discharge date. If this is
the case, it is best to be prepared and have your medication filled and ready for your return home from the hospital. You
may want to have your pain pills with you on your ride home if you are traveling a long distance.
While at Home:
+ Use medication only as directed.
* Remember medication takes time to work. Most oral pain relievers need at least 20 minutes to take effect.
+ Remember to take your pain medication before activity and at bedtime. Your provider may advise you to take
your pain medication at regular intervals (such as every 4 to 6 hours).
Be sure to get enough rest. Ifyou are having trouble sleeping, talk to your provider.
Use pillows to support you when you sleep and when you do your coughing and deep breathing exercises
Try using the alternative methods such as heating pads or cold therapy, walking, guided imagery tapes,
listening to soft music, changing your position in bed, aromatherapy, and massage can help relieve your pain.
Safe medication storage and disposal
Medications should be stored by patients in secure locations and excess pills should be disposed of properly, to
minimize the risk of diversion and inappropriate use. To find a prescription drug disposal location near you please
visit https://odcp.ky.gov
Third Party Apps and Epic
Patients of providers that use Epic software are able to configure 3rd party apps to retrieve parts of their health record
for their own personal use, including lab results, allergies, medications, and immunization history.
For instructions, visit: https://open.epic.com/Tutorial/PatientAuthentication.
Norton Care Call
If you are going home after leaving the hospital you will receive a Norton Care Call
+ Within 48 hours ofdischarge, you should receive an automated phone call from [PHONE-122] (Caller ID will read
Norton Care Call)
* You will be asked a few questions about your health and progress. Please answer the questions using the phone
keypad.
* Based on your answers, a Norton Healthcare team member may call you to offer help and other instructions.

Instructions
PATIENT INSTRUCTIONS
POST-ANESTHESIA
IMMEDIATELY FOLLOWING SURGERY: Do not drive, drink any alcohol, operate machinery, make important decisions,
or sign any legal paperwork for the next twenty four hours after surgery or while taking narcotic pain medications or
sedatives. You may experiencea sore throat, mild nausea, dizziness, drowsiness, or a headache. These symptoms are
normal after surgery and will subside in the next 24 hours. Ifyou develop severe nausea and vomiting, a severe
headache, or a high fever please notify your doctor immediately.
DO NOT TAKE TYLENOL WITH YOUR PERCOCET, DRINK PLENTY OF WATER, AND TAKE WITH FOOD.
CALL DR.KHALILY'S OFFICE IF YOU NOTICE ANY SIGNS OR SYMPTOMS OF INFECTION SUCH AS: INCREASED
REDNESS, SWELLING, FOUL SMELLING DRAINAGE, FEVER, RED STREAKS, OR CHILLS.

CONDITIONS OF ADMISSION AND
AUTHORIZATION FOR TREATMENT □ Norton Children's Hospital □ Norton Hospital □ Norton Audubon Hospital □ Norton Women’s and Children’s Hospital □ Norton Brownsboro Hospital □ Norton Children’s Medical Center
I. CONSENT TO DIAGNOSTIC TESTS, PROCEDURES, AND MEDICAL TREATMENT:
I voluntarily consent to care that involves routine diagnostic tests, procedures, and medical treatment as prescribed by my physician and performed by the facility. No guarantee has
been given by anyone as to the results that may be obtained. This consent includes testing for Hepatitis, Human Immunodeficiency Virus (HIV) or any other blood-borne infectious
diseases, if ordered for diagnostic purposes or due to an occupational exposure. I consent to photographing, videotaping, video monitoring and audio devices for medical, scientific,
safety or education purposes as well as for the purposes of identification. I understand that these will be stored in a secure manner that will protect my privacy. Images that identify me
will only be released when authorized by me or as needed to provide for my continued medical treatment or identification.
II. OTHER PRACTITIONERS AND SUPPLIERS OF SERVICES:
I understand and acknowledge that I may require the services of physicians, groups of physicians or other practitioners (such as nurses and physician assistants) who are not
employees of the facility, including, but not limited to, anesthesiologists, radiologists, emergency department physicians, certified registered nurse anesthetists, and other practitioners. I also understand that residents, fellows, medical students, and students of various health care fields may be involved in my care and that they are not employees of the
facility. I agree that the signing of this document does not in any way imply that Norton Healthcare is responsible for or assumes any liability for the activities of any such physicians or practitioners who are not its employees. When a physician, other practitioner or supplier of services bills me directly, I agree to pay the bill. I agree that the provisions regarding the
release of information and assignment of benefits set out in paragraphs III and V below shall apply not only to the facility but also to such physicians, practitioners and suppliers of
services and their claims for payment.
III. RELEASE OF INFORMATION:
I authorize the facility to notify my referring and treating physician(s), of my admission to the facility and to release any information about me as requested by such physician(s). I
authorize the facility and any other holder of medical or other information about me including medical information concerning drug related conditions, alcoholism, psychological
conditions, psychiatric conditions, and/or blood-borne infectious diseases, to release to the Social Security Administration, its intermediaries and its carriers, State agencies, the
review organization employed by my employer, or the employer of the insured member of my family, or any private third-party payor, as appropriate, any information required for the
completion of any claim for benefits arising out of services rendered to me either on an inpatient or outpatient basis. I further authorize the release of my social security number to the
manufacturer of any implanted medical device in accordance with the Medical Device Tracking Act of the Food and Drug Administration (FDA). I authorize the release of my HIV test
results to healthcare personnel in the event of an occupational exposure. If my injury is work-related, I authorize the facility and any other holder of medical or other information about
me to release from my medical record any information as requested by the company and/or its workers compensation administrator as indicated below:
COMPANY________________________________________________________________________ ADDRESS__________________________________________ IV. (initial)
THE FACILITY IS NOT RESPONSIBLE FOR LOSS OF PERSONAL ARTICLES:
I understand that the facility maintains a safe for the safekeeping of money and valuables and the facility shall not be liable for the loss of or damage to any money, jewelry,
documents, or any other items of personal property, unless deposited in the facility safe for safekeeping. Furthermore, I accept full responsibility for items of personal property kept in
my possession.

V. ASSIGNMENT OF BENEFITS:
I agree to the assignment of all third-party benefits to the facility and agree to pay the facility for all charges not covered by third-party payors. In the case of outpatient services I agree
that this document shall remain in full force and effect until specifically revoked by me in writing. Any sums not paid by a third-party payor are my obligation.
VI. RELEASE OF INSURANCE INFORMATION TO FACILITY:
I agree to the release by my insurance carrier to the facility and the facility's billing service of any eligibility and utilization data concerning my insurance coverage which the facility and/or its billing
supplier may require. I authorize the facility to file an appeal of a payment denial and/or request a hearing regarding any denial of payment for treatment provided to me. I further authorize the facility
to present proof, utilize facility records and my records and documentation for appeals and hearings.
VII. PAYMENT OF FACILITY BILLS WHEN DUE:
I am liable for the payment of the account of the facility and I am obligated to pay the account of the facility, in accordance with the regular rates and terms of the facility. If my injury is work-related, I am further obligated to pay the account of the facility in the event my employer or its third-party administrator denies payment for workers compensation. It is understood that the uninsured portion of bills are payable at the end of each week and in full upon discharge from the facility. I understand that after reasonable notice, delinquent
accounts may be turned over to a collection agency and/or an attorney for collection. Should it be necessary to place this account in the hands of an attorney for collection, I agree to
pay the costs of collection, including any court costs and a reasonable fee to the attorney employed by the facility to collect the account.
I agree that the facility, its employees, agents, attorneys and collection agencies, may call the cell number I provide for any reason, including but not limited to inquiring about the
status and collection of my account. I also expressly authorize that each of them may use any mechanism, including but not limited to automatic dialing, artificial and prerecorded
voice systems. VIII.HIV/AIDS INFORMATION: I acknowledge receipt of an HIV/AIDS informational brochure.
IX. SMOKING CESSATION COUNSELING (18 YEARS AND OLDER): I acknowledge receipt of smoking cessation counseling informational handout.
X. PRIVACY NOTICE: I acknowledge that a copy of Norton's Notice of Privacy Practices has been made available to me.
XI. PATIENT BILL OF RIGHTS: I acknowledge that a copy of the Patient Bill of Rights has been made available to me.
The undersigned agrees that a copy of this release and assignment may be used in place of the original copy. The undersigned certifies that he/she has read and agrees to this
agreement and has received a copy. The undersigned certifies that the patient is unable to consent or is a minor and the undersigned hereby consents to the above as indicated below.
If the patient is not the insured, or if the patient does not pay the account in full, the undersigned agrees to be financially responsible for the charges detailed above, individually or jointly with the
patient.

TO THE PATIENT: Anesthesia is necessary to facilitate the recommended surgicar, meaical or diagnostic pracedure(s)
you have consented to undergo and the use of invasive monitors (which are devices that enter the body to aid the
physician inmaking decisions regarding apatient’s vital functions) may be necessary to assist with theprovision of the
anesthesia. You have the right, as a patient, to be informed about the provision of anesthesia and invasive monitors in
connection with thesurgical, medical or diagnostic procedure({s) to be used to diagnose or treat your condition,
/ ! understand that, in connection with the surgical, medical, or diagnostic procedure(s) used to diagnose or treat
‘ny condition, the physicians and certified registered nurse anesthetists of Professional Anesthesia Services of Kentucky,
PLLC, (my “Anesthesia Provider(s)”) and such associates, technical assistants and other health care providers as they may
deel necessary, will be the providers of the anesthesia services and invasive monitors, if necessary.
‘A physician who is not affiliated with Professional Anesthesia Services of Kentucky, PLLC (my “Treating Physician”),
has already explained to me what my condition is, and | have already consented to the surgical, medical or diagnostic
procedufe(s) recommended by my Treating Physician to diagnose or treat my condition.
' | understand that myTreating Physician and/orAnesthesia Provider may discover other or different conditions
which require additional or different procedures than those planned. | understand that the type of anesthesia service
may have to be changed, possibly without explanation to me. |authorize the Anesthesia Providers to provide such
other anesthesia services which are advisable in their professional judgment.
RISKSAND HAZARDS ASSOCIATED WITH ANESTHESIA:
| understand that all forms of anesthesia involve some risks and no guarantees or promises can be made
concerning the results of my procedure or treatment. Just as there may be risks and hazards in continuing my present
condition without treatment, there are also risks and hazards related to the performance of the surgical, medical or
diagnostic procedure(s), including the anesthesia planned for me. | realize that severe complications with anesthesia can
occur, including the potential for infection, blood clots in veins and lungs, hemorrhage, drug reactions, respiratory
problems, cardiac/cardiovascular/other major organ problems, loss of limb function or sensation, paralysis, stroke, brain
damage and even death. |further understand that, in addition to the complications noted above, the following risks and
hazards may occur in connection with the forms of anesthesia listed below:
GENERAL ANESTHESIA
Description: Total unconscious state, possible placement ofa tube into the windpipe
Technique: Drug injected into the bloodstream, breathed into the lungs, or administered by other routes
Risks: Permanent organ damage; memory dysfunction/memory joss; minor discomfort; mouth, jaw or throat pain;
hoarseness; injury to mouth, teeth, lips, gums, vocal cords, or eyes; need for post-operative ventilation; awareness under
anesthesia; and brain damage.
c EPIDURAL/ SPINAL
Description: Temporary decrease or loss of feeling and/or movement to lower part of body
Technique: Drug injected through a needle/catheter placed either directly into the spinal canal or immediately outside the
spinal canal
Risks: Headache; chronic pain; persistent back pain; bleeding/epidural hematoma; infection; nerve injury or damage; “total
spinal”; potential to convert to a general anesthetic if the block fails or the procedure outlasts the block; and/or brain damage.
coMONITORED ANESTHESIA CARE WITH SEDATION (MAC or Conscious Sedation)
Description: Reduced anxiety and pain, partial or total amnesia
Technique: Drug injected into the bloodstream, breathed into the lungs, or administered by other routes producing a semiconscious state. This may include the administration of drugs to help alleviate anxiety, either alone or as a supplement to a
local or regional technique.
Risks: Permanent organ damage; brain damage; memory dysfunction/memory loss; potential to convert to generalanesthetic
if the sedation is not adequate; an unconscious state; and/or difficulty with breathing. Please know that MAC is a vigilant
monitoring of a patient’s vital functions while undergoing therapeutic or diagnostic procedures.

s/MAJOR / MINOR REGIONAL NERVEBLOCK ANESTHESIA
Right Left Keterscalend Supraclavicular {nfraclavicular Axillary Wrist Digital
Femoral Saphenous Popliteal Sciatic Ankle Eye
Description: Temporary loss of feeling and/or movement of a limb
Technique: Local anesthetic injected via a needle with nerve twitch monitor and/ or ultrasound guidance providing loss of
sensation.to the limb or area of the operation
Risks: Infection; convulsions; weakness; persistent numbness; residual pain; injury to blood vessels (eye block-loss of vision);
inability to breathe on your own which may require breathing assistance upto and including placement of a tube into the
windpipe; collapsed lung; hematoma; temporary paralysis of the diaphragm; chronic pain; and medical necessity to convert
to general anesthesia; nerve damage
RISKS AND HAZARDS ASSOCIATED WITH INVASIVE MONITORS:
Invasive monitors are devices that enter the body to aid the physician in making decisions regarding the patient’s vital
functions that cannot be obtained by non-invasive monitors. Certain risks involved in using invasive monitofs include:
injuries to blood vessels and/or theheart; infection; puncture of lung; collapse of the lung; injury to nerves; stroke; loss of
digits; anxiety and/or discomfort. ‘
ADDITIONAL RISKS TO SPECIFIC SURGERIES:
While complications are rare, different surgeries carry special risks. For example, spinal surgery has specific risks which
you and your surgeon may have already discussed, such as the risk of blindness after surgery. Blindness can affect one or
both eyes, may bepartial or complete, temporary or rarely permanent. This risk is related to prone (belly down) position,
as well as multiple other factors. Some risks are not necessarily dependent on the surgery or anesthesia alone. Your age,
weight, and other health conditions may also affect your risk. Please do not hesitate to ask your anesthesiologist any
questions you may have regarding specific risks to your surgery. Additional risks discussed:

read this form or had it read to me, that | understand the risks, alternatives and expected results of the anesthesia services
and that |had ample time to ask questions and to consider my decision.
